## [Apr 17 - Apr 23, 2023](/content/2023/16/README.md)

### Continuous Integration

*   [go-test-coverage (‚≠ê6)](https://github.com/vladopajic/go-test-coverage) - Tool and GitHub action which reports issues when test coverage is below set threshold.

### Caches

*   [imcache (‚≠ê40)](https://github.com/erni27/imcache) - A generic in-memory cache Go library. It supports expiration, sliding expiration, max entries limit, eviction callbacks and sharding.
*   [theine (‚≠ê40)](https://github.com/Yiling-J/theine-go) - High performance, near optimal in-memory cache with proactive TTL expiration and generics.

### Images

*   [color-extractor (‚≠ê55)](https://github.com/marekm4/color-extractor) - Dominant color extractor with no external dependencies.

### Web Frameworks

*   [Pulse (‚≠ê20)](https://github.com/gopulse/pulse) - Pulse is an HTTP web framework written in Go (Golang)

## [Apr 10 - Apr 16, 2023](/content/2023/15/README.md)

### Code Analysis / Libraries for creating HTTP middlewares

*   [blanket](https://gitlab.com/verygoodsoftwarenotvirus/blanket) - blanket is a tool that helps you catch functions which don't have direct unit tests in your Go packages.

## [Apr 03 - Apr 09, 2023](/content/2023/14/README.md)

### Markup Languages

*   [htmlyaml (‚≠ê2)](https://github.com/nikolaydubina/htmlyaml) -  Rich rendering of YAML as HTML in Go

### Utilities

*   [just (‚≠ê20)](https://github.com/kazhuravlev/just) - Just a collection of useful functions for working with generic data structures.

### Twitter / Libraries for creating HTTP middlewares

*   [@GoDiscussions](https://twitter.com/GoDiscussions)

### Websites / Libraries for creating HTTP middlewares

*   [Golang Weekly](https://discu.eu/weekly/golang/) - Each monday projects, tutorials and articles about Go.

### Utilities

*   [contextplus (‚≠ê17)](https://github.com/contextplus/contextplus) - Package contextplus provide more easy to use functions for contexts.

## [Mar 13 - Mar 19, 2023](/content/2023/11/README.md)

### Authentication and OAuth

*   [go-jose (‚≠ê111)](https://github.com/go-jose/go-jose) - Fairly complete implementation of the JOSE working group's JSON Web Token, JSON Web Signatures, and JSON Web Encryption specs.

### NoSQL Database Drivers

*   [redis (‚≠ê17k)](https://github.com/redis/go-redis) - Redis client for Golang.

### JSON

*   [htmljson (‚≠ê3)](https://github.com/nikolaydubina/htmljson) - Rich rendering of JSON as HTML in Go.

### Science and Data Analysis

*   [gograph (‚≠ê21)](https://github.com/hmdsefi/gograph) -  A golang generic graph library that provides mathematical graph-theory and algorithms.

### Third-party APIs

*   [go-openai (‚≠ê4.1k)](https://github.com/sashabaranov/go-openai) - OpenAI ChatGPT, DALL¬∑E, Whisper API library for Go.

### Utilities

*   [watchhttp (‚≠ê22)](https://github.com/nikolaydubina/watchhttp) - Run command periodically and expose latest STDOUT or its rich delta as HTTP endpoint.

## [Mar 06 - Mar 12, 2023](/content/2023/10/README.md)

### Advanced Console UIs

*   [go-palette (‚≠ê8)](https://github.com/abusomani/go-palette) - Go library that provides elegant and convenient style definitions using ANSI colors. Fully compatible & wraps the [fmt library](https://pkg.go.dev/fmt) for nice terminal layouts.

### JSON

*   [jsonhandlers (‚≠ê1)](https://github.com/abusomani/jsonhandlers) - JSON library to expose simple handlers that lets you easily read and write json from various sources.

### Third-party APIs

*   [openaigo (‚≠ê229)](https://github.com/otiai10/openaigo) - OpenAI GPT3/GPT3.5 ChatGPT API client library for Go.

### Go Generate Tools / Libraries for creating HTTP middlewares

*   [options-gen (‚≠ê38)](https://github.com/kazhuravlev/options-gen) - Functional options described by Dave Cheney's post "Functional options for friendly APIs".

## [Feb 20 - Feb 26, 2023](/content/2023/8/README.md)

### Bot Building

*   [bot (‚≠ê72)](https://github.com/go-telegram/bot) - Zero-dependencies Telegram Bot library with additional UI components

### Build Automation

*   [xc (‚≠ê803)](https://github.com/joerdav/xc) - Task runner with README.md defined tasks, executable markdown.

### Database Tools

*   [onedump (‚≠ê17)](https://github.com/liweiyi88/onedump) - Database backup from different drivers to different destinations with one command and configuration.

### Error Handling

*   [Fault (‚≠ê123)](https://github.com/Southclaws/fault) - An ergonomic mechanism for wrapping errors in order to facilitate structured metadata and context for error values.

### Messaging

*   [Watermill (‚≠ê5.5k)](https://github.com/ThreeDotsLabs/watermill) - Working efficiently with message streams. Building event driven applications, enabling event sourcing, RPC over messages, sagas. Can use conventional pub/sub implementations like Kafka or RabbitMQ, but also HTTP or MySQL binlog.

### Security

*   [booster (‚≠ê339)](https://github.com/anatol/booster) - Fast initramfs generator with full-disk encryption support.

### Other Software / Libraries for creating HTTP middlewares

*   [hotswap (‚≠ê213)](https://github.com/edwingeng/hotswap) - A complete solution to reload your go code without restarting your server, interrupting or blocking any ongoing procedure.

### E-books for purchase / Libraries for creating HTTP middlewares

*   [Lets-Go-Further](https://lets-go-further.alexedwards.net) - Advanced patterns for building APIs and web applications in Go.

### Miscellaneous Data Structures and Algorithms

*   [gogu (‚≠ê65)](https://github.com/esimov/gogu) - A comprehensive, reusable and efficient concurrent-safe generics utility functions and data structures library.

### Interfaces to Multiple Backends

*   [go-transaction-manager (‚≠ê33)](https://github.com/avito-tech/go-transaction-manager) - Transaction manager with multiple adapters (sql, sqlx, gorm, mongo, ...) controls transaction boundaries.

### Security

*   [teler-waf (‚≠ê127)](https://github.com/kitabisa/teler-waf) - teler-waf is a Go HTTP middleware that provide teler IDS functionality to protect against web-based attacks and improve the security of Go-based web applications. It is highly configurable and easy to integrate into existing Go applications.

## [Oct 17 - Oct 23, 2022](/content/2022/42/README.md)

### Authentication and OAuth

*   [authboss (‚≠ê3.4k)](https://github.com/volatiletech/authboss) - Modular authentication system for the web. It tries to remove as much boilerplate and "hard things" as possible so that each time you start a new web project in Go, you can plug it in, configure it, and start building your app without having to build an authentication system each time.
*   [casbin (‚≠ê14k)](https://github.com/hsluoyz/casbin) - Authorization library that supports access control models like ACL, RBAC, and ABAC.
*   [cookiestxt (‚≠ê12)](https://github.com/mengzhuo/cookiestxt) - provides a parser of cookies.txt file format.
*   [go-guardian (‚≠ê450)](https://github.com/shaj13/go-guardian) - Go-Guardian is a golang library that provides a simple, clean, and idiomatic way to create powerful modern API and web authentication that supports LDAP, Basic, Bearer token, and Certificate based authentication.
*   [gosession (‚≠ê46)](http://github.com/Kwynto/gosession) - This is quick session for net/http in GoLang. This package is perhaps the best implementation of the session mechanism, or at least it tries to become one.
*   [jeff (‚≠ê256)](https://github.com/abraithwaite/jeff) - Simple, flexible, secure, and idiomatic web session management with pluggable backends.
*   [jwt (‚≠ê594)](https://github.com/cristalhq/jwt) - Safe, simple, and fast JSON Web Tokens for Go.
*   [oauth2 (‚≠ê4.7k)](https://github.com/golang/oauth2) - Successor of goauth2. Generic OAuth 2.0 package that comes with JWT, Google APIs, Compute Engine, and App Engine support.
*   [permissions2 (‚≠ê480)](https://github.com/xyproto/permissions2) - Library for keeping track of users, login states, and permissions. Uses secure cookies and bcrypt.

### Bot Building

*   [go-sarah (‚≠ê253)](https://github.com/oklahomer/go-sarah) - Framework to build a bot for desired chat services including LINE, Slack, Gitter, and more.
*   [go-tgbot (‚≠ê118)](https://github.com/olebedev/go-tgbot) - Pure Golang Telegram Bot API wrapper, generated from swagger file, session-based router, and middleware.
*   [telebot (‚≠ê3k)](https://github.com/tucnak/telebot) - Telegram bot framework is written in Go.

### Build Automation

*   [realize (‚≠ê4.4k)](https://github.com/tockins/realize) - Go build a system with file watchers and live to reload. Run, build and watch file changes with custom paths.

### Advanced Console UIs

*   [aurora (‚≠ê1.3k)](https://github.com/logrusorgru/aurora) - ANSI terminal colors that support fmt.Printf/Sprintf.
*   [simpletable (‚≠ê441)](https://github.com/alexeyco/simpletable) - Simple tables in a terminal with Go.
*   [uilive (‚≠ê1.5k)](https://github.com/gosuri/uilive) - Library for updating terminal output in real time.

### Standard CLI

*   [acmd (‚≠ê80)](https://github.com/cristalhq/acmd) - Simple, useful, and opinionated CLI package in Go.
*   [command-chain (‚≠ê40)](https://github.com/rainu/go-command-chain) - A go library for configure and run command chains - such as pipelining in unix shells.
*   [go-andotp (‚≠ê22)](https://github.com/grijul/go-andotp) - A CLI program to encrypt/decrypt [andOTP (‚≠ê3.7k)](https://github.com/andOTP/andOTP) files. Can be used as a library as well.
*   [go-getoptions (‚≠ê46)](https://github.com/DavidGamba/go-getoptions) - Go option parser inspired by the flexibility of Perl‚Äôs GetOpt::Long.
*   [sflags (‚≠ê147)](https://github.com/octago/sflags) - Struct based flags generator for flag, urfave/cli, pflag, cobra, kingpin, and other libraries.
*   [wmenu (‚≠ê187)](https://github.com/dixonwille/wmenu) - Easy to use menu structure for cli applications that prompt users to make choices.

## [Apr 04 - Apr 10, 2022](/content/2022/14/README.md)

### Bit-packing and Compression

*   [crunch (‚≠ê84)](https://github.com/superwhiskers/crunch) - Go package implementing buffers for handling various datatypes easily.
*   [go-ef (‚≠ê28)](https://github.com/amallia/go-ef) - A Go implementation of the Elias-Fano encoding.
*   [roaring (‚≠ê2k)](https://github.com/RoaringBitmap/roaring) - Go package implementing compressed bitsets.

### Bloom and Cuckoo Filters

*   [cuckoo-filter (‚≠ê251)](https://github.com/linvon/cuckoo-filter) - Cuckoo filter: a comprehensive cuckoo filter, which is configurable and space optimized compared with other implements, and all features mentioned in original paper is available.
*   [cuckoofilter (‚≠ê982)](https://github.com/seiflotfy/cuckoofilter) - Cuckoo filter: a good alternative to a counting bloom filter implemented in Go.
*   [ring (‚≠ê130)](https://github.com/TheTannerRyan/ring) - Go implementation of a high performance, thread safe bloom filter.

### Data Structure and Algorithm Collections

*   [algorithms (‚≠ê712)](https://github.com/shady831213/algorithms) - Algorithms and data structures.CLRS study.
*   [go-datastructures (‚≠ê6.8k)](https://github.com/Workiva/go-datastructures) - Collection of useful, performant, and thread-safe data structures.
*   [gods (‚≠ê14k)](https://github.com/emirpasic/gods) - Go Data Structures. Containers, Sets, Lists, Stacks, Maps, BidiMaps, Trees, HashSet etc.
*   [gostl (‚≠ê840)](https://github.com/liyue201/gostl) - Data structure and algorithm library for go, designed to provide functions similar to C++ STL.

### Iterators

### Nullable Types

*   [nan (‚≠ê67)](https://github.com/kak-tus/nan) - Zero allocation Nullable structures in one library with handy conversion functions, marshallers and unmarshallers.

### Queues

*   [deque (‚≠ê121)](https://github.com/edwingeng/deque) - A highly optimized double-ended queue.
*   [deque (‚≠ê443)](https://github.com/gammazero/deque) - Fast ring-buffer deque (double-ended queue).

*   [memlog (‚≠ê82)](https://github.com/embano1/memlog) - An easy to use, lightweight, thread-safe and append-only in-memory data structure inspired by Apache Kafka.

### Sets

*   [dsu (‚≠ê11)](https://github.com/ihebu/dsu) - Disjoint Set data structure implementation in Go.

*   [set (‚≠ê22)](https://github.com/StudioSol/set) - Simple set data structure implementation in Go using LinkedHashMap.

### Text Analysis

*   [bleve (‚≠ê9k)](https://github.com/blevesearch/bleve) - Modern text indexing library for go.
*   [go-adaptive-radix-tree (‚≠ê281)](https://github.com/plar/go-adaptive-radix-tree) - Go implementation of Adaptive Radix Tree.
*   [go-edlib (‚≠ê382)](https://github.com/hbollon/go-edlib) - Go string comparison and edit distance algorithms library (Levenshtein, LCS, Hamming, Damerau levenshtein, Jaro-Winkler, etc.) compatible with Unicode.
*   [trie (‚≠ê641)](https://github.com/derekparker/trie) - Trie implementation in Go.

### Trees

*   [hashsplit (‚≠ê14)](http://github.com/bobg/hashsplit) - Split byte streams into chunks, and arrange chunks into trees, with boundaries determined by content, not position.
*   [merkle (‚≠ê11)](https://github.com/bobg/merkle) - Space-efficient computation of Merkle root hashes and inclusion proofs.

### Pipes

*   [ordered-concurrently (‚≠ê22)](https://github.com/tejzpr/ordered-concurrently) - Go module that processes work concurrently and returns output in a channel in the order of input.
*   [parapipe (‚≠ê23)](https://github.com/nazar256/parapipe) - FIFO Pipeline which parallels execution on each stage while maintaining the order of messages and results.
*   [pipeline (‚≠ê46)](https://github.com/hyfather/pipeline) - An implementation of pipelines with fan-in and fan-out.

### Caches

*   [2q (‚≠ê22)](https://github.com/floatdrop/2q) - 2Q in-memory cache implementation.
*   [bcache (‚≠ê116)](https://github.com/iwanbk/bcache) - Eventually consistent distributed in-memory cache Go library.
*   [couchcache (‚≠ê58)](https://github.com/codingsince1985/couchcache) - RESTful caching micro-service backed by Couchbase server.
*   [fastcache (‚≠ê1.7k)](https://github.com/VictoriaMetrics/fastcache) - fast thread-safe inmemory cache for big number of entries. Minimizes GC overhead.
*   [GCache (‚≠ê2.3k)](https://github.com/bluele/gcache) - Cache library with support for expirable Cache, LFU, LRU and ARC.
*   [gdcache (‚≠ê11)](https://github.com/ulovecode/gdcache) - A pure non-intrusive cache library implemented by golang, you can use it to implement your own distributed cache.
*   [go-mcache (‚≠ê86)](https://github.com/OrlovEvgeny/go-mcache) - Fast in-memory key:value store/cache library. Pointer caches.
*   [groupcache (‚≠ê12k)](https://github.com/golang/groupcache) - Groupcache is a caching and cache-filling library, intended as a replacement for memcached in many cases.
*   [remember-go (‚≠ê125)](https://github.com/rocketlaunchr/remember-go) - A universal interface for caching slow database queries (backed by redis, memcached, ristretto, or in-memory).
*   [timedmap (‚≠ê54)](https://github.com/zekroTJA/timedmap) - Map with expiring key-value pairs.
*   [ttlcache (‚≠ê616)](https://github.com/jellydator/ttlcache) - An in-memory cache with item expiration and generics.
*   [ttlcache (‚≠ê9)](https://github.com/cheshir/ttlcache) - In-memory key value storage with TTL for each record.

### Databases Implemented in Go

*   [badger (‚≠ê12k)](https://github.com/dgraph-io/badger) - Fast key-value store in Go.
*   [bbolt (‚≠ê6.4k)](https://github.com/etcd-io/bbolt) - An embedded key/value database for Go.
*   [Bitcask](https://git.mills.io/prologic/bitcask) - Bitcask is an embeddable, persistent and fast key-value (KV) database written in pure Go with predictable read/write performance, low latency and high throughput thanks to the bitcask on-disk layout (LSM+WAL).
*   [buntdb (‚≠ê4.1k)](https://github.com/tidwall/buntdb) - Fast, embeddable, in-memory key/value database for Go with custom indexing and spatial support.
*   [clover (‚≠ê366)](https://github.com/ostafen/clover) - A lightweight document-oriented NoSQL database written in pure Golang.
*   [nutsdb (‚≠ê2.8k)](https://github.com/xujiajun/nutsdb) - Nutsdb is a simple, fast, embeddable, persistent key/value store written in pure Go. It supports fully serializable transactions and many data structures such as list, set, sorted set.
*   [pudge (‚≠ê337)](https://github.com/recoilme/pudge) - Fast and simple key/value store written using Go's standard library.
*   [unitdb (‚≠ê105)](https://github.com/unit-io/unitdb) - Fast timeseries database for IoT, realtime messaging applications. Access unitdb with pubsub over tcp or websocket using github.com/unit-io/unitd application.

### Database Tools

*   [clickhouse-bulk (‚≠ê413)](https://github.com/nikepan/clickhouse-bulk) - Collects small inserts and sends big requests to ClickHouse servers.

### Interfaces to Multiple Backends

*   [cayley (‚≠ê15k)](https://github.com/google/cayley) - Graph database with support for multiple backends.
*   [dsc (‚≠ê26)](https://github.com/viant/dsc) - Datastore connectivity for SQL, NoSQL, structured files.
*   [gokv (‚≠ê532)](https://github.com/philippgille/gokv) - Simple key-value store abstraction and implementations for Go (Redis, Consul, etcd, bbolt, BadgerDB, LevelDB, Memcached, DynamoDB, S3, PostgreSQL, MongoDB, CockroachDB and many more).

### Relational Database Drivers

*   [avatica (‚≠ê109)](https://github.com/apache/calcite-avatica-go) - Apache Avatica/Phoenix SQL driver for database/sql.
*   [bgc (‚≠ê19)](https://github.com/viant/bgc) - Datastore Connectivity for BigQuery for go.
*   [firebirdsql (‚≠ê196)](https://github.com/nakagami/firebirdsql) - Firebird RDBMS SQL driver for Go.
*   [go-adodb (‚≠ê132)](https://github.com/mattn/go-adodb) - Microsoft ActiveX Object DataBase driver for go that uses database/sql.
*   [go-mssqldb (‚≠ê1.7k)](https://github.com/denisenkom/go-mssqldb) - Microsoft MSSQL driver for Go.
*   [go-oci8 (‚≠ê603)](https://github.com/mattn/go-oci8) - Oracle driver for go that uses database/sql.
*   [go-sql-driver/mysql (‚≠ê13k)](https://github.com/go-sql-driver/mysql) - MySQL driver for Go.
*   [go-sqlite3 (‚≠ê6.5k)](https://github.com/mattn/go-sqlite3) - SQLite3 driver for go that uses database/sql.
*   [godror (‚≠ê435)](https://github.com/godror/godror) - Oracle driver for Go, using the ODPI-C driver.
*   [gofreetds (‚≠ê107)](https://github.com/minus5/gofreetds) - Microsoft MSSQL driver. Go wrapper over [FreeTDS](https://www.freetds.org).
*   [pgx (‚≠ê7k)](https://github.com/jackc/pgx) - PostgreSQL driver supporting features beyond those exposed by database/sql.
*   [pig (‚≠ê13)](https://github.com/alexeyco/pig) - Simple [pgx (‚≠ê7k)](https://github.com/jackc/pgx) wrapper to execute and [scan (‚≠ê891)](https://github.com/georgysavva/scany) query results easily.
*   [pq (‚≠ê8k)](https://github.com/lib/pq) - Pure Go Postgres driver for database/sql.
*   [Sqinn-Go (‚≠ê135)](https://github.com/cvilsmeier/sqinn-go) - SQLite with pure Go.
*   [sqlhooks (‚≠ê606)](https://github.com/qustavo/sqlhooks) - Attach hooks to any database/sql driver.

*   [Kivik (‚≠ê258)](https://github.com/go-kivik/kivik) - Kivik provides a common Go and GopherJS client library for CouchDB, PouchDB, and similar databases.
*   [mgm (‚≠ê644)](https://github.com/kamva/mgm) - MongoDB model-based ODM for Go (based on official MongoDB driver).
*   [mgo (‚≠ê2k)](https://github.com/globalsign/mgo) - (unmaintained) MongoDB driver for the Go language that implements a rich and well tested selection of features under a very simple API following standard Go idioms.
*   [mongo-go-driver (‚≠ê7.3k)](https://github.com/mongodb/mongo-go-driver) - Official MongoDB driver for the Go language.

### Translation

*   [go-i18n (‚≠ê2.4k)](https://github.com/nicksnyder/go-i18n/) - Package and an accompanying tool to work with localized text.
*   [go-localize (‚≠ê52)](https://github.com/m1/go-localize) - Simple and easy to use i18n (Internationalization and localization) engine - used for translating locale strings.

*   [icu (‚≠ê21)](https://github.com/goodsign/icu) - Cgo binding for icu4c C library detection and conversion functions. Guaranteed compatibility with version 50.1.
*   [iuliia-go (‚≠ê39)](https://github.com/mehanizm/iuliia-go) - Transliterate Cyrillic ‚Üí Latin in every possible way.
*   [t (‚≠ê14)](https://github.com/youthlin/t) - Another i18n pkg for golang, which follows GNU gettext style and supports .po/.mo files: `t.T (gettext)`, `t.N (ngettext)`, etc. And it contains a cmd tool [xtemplate (‚≠ê14)](https://github.com/youthlin/t/blob/main/cmd/xtemplate), which can extract messages as a pot file from text/html template.

*   [envh (‚≠ê96)](https://github.com/antham/envh) - Helpers to manage environment variables.
*   [fig (‚≠ê266)](https://github.com/kkyr/fig) - Tiny library for reading configuration from a file and from environment variables (with validation & defaults).
*   [gcfg (‚≠ê162)](https://github.com/go-gcfg/gcfg) - read INI-style configuration files into Go structs; supports user-defined types and subsections.
*   [genv (‚≠ê32)](https://github.com/sakirsensoy/genv) - Read environment variables easily with dotenv support.
*   [go-aws-ssm (‚≠ê54)](https://github.com/PaddleHQ/go-aws-ssm) - Go package that fetches parameters from AWS System Manager - Parameter Store.
*   [go-conf (‚≠ê8)](https://github.com/ThomasObenaus/go-conf) - Simple library for application configuration based on annotated structs. It supports reading the configuration from environment variables, config files and command line parameters.
*   [go-ini (‚≠ê9)](https://github.com/subpop/go-ini) - A Go package that marshals and unmarshals INI-files.
*   [go-ssm-config (‚≠ê17)](https://github.com/ianlopshire/go-ssm-config) - Go utility for loading configuration parameters from AWS SSM (Parameter Store).
*   [go-up (‚≠ê39)](https://github.com/ufoscout/go-up) - A simple configuration library with recursive placeholders resolution and no magic.
*   [goConfig (‚≠ê3)](https://github.com/crgimenes/goConfig) - Parses a struct as input and populates the fields of this struct with parameters from command line, environment variables and configuration file.
*   [godotenv (‚≠ê6k)](https://github.com/joho/godotenv) - Go port of Ruby's dotenv library (Loads environment variables from `.env`).
*   [gofigure (‚≠ê65)](https://github.com/ian-kent/gofigure) - Go application configuration made easy.
*   [gone/jconf (‚≠ê45)](https://github.com/One-com/gone/tree/master/jconf) - Modular JSON configuration. Keep you config structs along with the code they configure and delegate parsing to submodules without sacrificing full config serialization.
*   [gonfig (‚≠ê6)](https://github.com/milad-abbasi/gonfig) - Tag-based configuration parser which loads values from different providers into typesafe struct.
*   [gookit/config (‚≠ê453)](https://github.com/gookit/config) - application config manage(load,get,set). support JSON, YAML, TOML, INI, HCL. multi file load, data override merge.
*   [hjson (‚≠ê298)](https://github.com/hjson/hjson-go) - Human JSON, a configuration file format for humans. Relaxed syntax, fewer mistakes, more comments.
*   [hocon (‚≠ê56)](https://github.com/gurkankaymak/hocon) - Configuration library for working with the HOCON(a human-friendly JSON superset) format, supports features like environment variables, referencing other values, comments and multiple files.
*   [ingo (‚≠ê36)](https://github.com/schachmat/ingo) - Flags persisted in an ini-like config file.
*   [ini (‚≠ê3.2k)](https://github.com/go-ini/ini) - Go package to read and write INI files.
*   [ini (‚≠ê12)](https://github.com/wlevene/ini) - INI Parser & Write Library, Unmarshal to Struct,Marshal to Json,Write File,watch file.
*   [joshbetz/config (‚≠ê214)](https://github.com/joshbetz/config) - Small configuration library for Go that parses environment variables, JSON files, and reloads automatically on SIGHUP.
*   [kelseyhightower/envconfig (‚≠ê4.5k)](https://github.com/kelseyhightower/envconfig) - Go library for managing configuration data from environment variables.
*   [koanf (‚≠ê1.8k)](https://github.com/knadh/koanf) - Light weight, extensible library for reading config in Go applications. Built in support for JSON, TOML, YAML, env, command line.
*   [konfig (‚≠ê634)](https://github.com/lalamove/konfig) - Composable, observable and performant config handling for Go for the distributed processing era.
*   [mini (‚≠ê34)](https://github.com/sasbury/mini) - Golang package for parsing ini-style configuration files.
*   [nasermirzaei89/env (‚≠ê10)](https://github.com/nasermirzaei89/env) - Simple useful package for read environment variables.
*   [onion (‚≠ê113)](https://github.com/goraz/onion) - Layer based configuration for Go, Supports JSON, TOML, YAML, properties, etcd, env, and encryption using PGP.
*   [piper (‚≠ê7)](https://github.com/Yiling-J/piper) - Viper wrapper with config inheritance and key generation.
*   [store (‚≠ê267)](https://github.com/tucnak/store) - Lightweight configuration manager for Go.
*   [swap (‚≠ê8)](https://github.com/oblq/swap) - Instantiate/configure structs recursively, based on build environment. (YAML, TOML, JSON and env).
*   [typenv (‚≠ê9)](https://github.com/diegomarangoni/typenv) - Minimalistic, zero dependency, typed environment variables library.
*   [uConfig (‚≠ê59)](https://github.com/omeid/uconfig) - Lightweight, zero-dependency, and extendable configuration management.
*   [viper (‚≠ê23k)](https://github.com/spf13/viper) - Go configuration with fangs.
*   [xdg (‚≠ê360)](https://github.com/adrg/xdg) - Go implementation of the [XDG Base Directory Specification](https://specifications.freedesktop.org/basedir-spec/basedir-spec-latest.html) and [XDG user directories](https://wiki.archlinux.org/index.php/XDG_user_directories).
*   [xdg (‚≠ê73)](https://github.com/OpenPeeDeeP/xdg) - Cross platform package that follows the [XDG Standard](https://standards.freedesktop.org/basedir-spec/basedir-spec-latest.html).

### Miscellaneous Data Structures and Algorithms

*   [concurrent-writer (‚≠ê48)](https://github.com/free/concurrent-writer) - Highly concurrent drop-in replacement for `bufio.Writer`.
*   [conjungo (‚≠ê111)](https://github.com/InVisionApp/conjungo) - A small, powerful and flexible merge library.
*   [count-min-log (‚≠ê60)](https://github.com/seiflotfy/count-min-log) - Go implementation Count-Min-Log sketch: Approximately counting with approximate counters (Like Count-Min sketch but using less memory).
*   [fsm (‚≠ê40)](https://github.com/cocoonspace/fsm) - Finite-State Machine package.
*   [go-geoindex (‚≠ê347)](https://github.com/hailocab/go-geoindex) - In-memory geo index.
*   [go-rquad (‚≠ê123)](https://github.com/aurelien-rainone/go-rquad) - Region quadtrees with efficient point location and neighbour finding.
*   [gofal (‚≠ê17)](https://github.com/xxjwxc/gofal) - fractional api for Go.
*   [gota (‚≠ê2.6k)](https://github.com/kniren/gota) - Implementation of dataframes, series, and data wrangling methods for Go.
*   [hide (‚≠ê53)](https://github.com/emvi/hide) - ID type with marshalling to/from hash to prevent sending IDs to clients.
*   [hilbert (‚≠ê261)](https://github.com/google/hilbert) - Go package for mapping values to and from space-filling curves, such as Hilbert and Peano curves.
*   [hyperloglog (‚≠ê841)](https://github.com/axiomhq/hyperloglog) - HyperLogLog implementation with Sparse, LogLog-Beta bias correction and TailCut space reduction.

### SQL Query Builders

*   [jet (‚≠ê1.1k)](https://github.com/go-jet/jet) - Framework for writing type-safe SQL queries in Go, with ability to easily convert database query result into desired arbitrary object structure.
*   [ormlite (‚≠ê7)](https://github.com/pupizoid/ormlite) - Lightweight package containing some ORM-like features and helpers for sqlite databases.
*   [ozzo-dbx (‚≠ê594)](https://github.com/go-ozzo/ozzo-dbx) - Powerful data retrieval methods as well as DB-agnostic query building capabilities.
*   [qry (‚≠ê28)](https://github.com/HnH/qry) - Tool that generates constants from files with raw SQL queries.
*   [sq (‚≠ê190)](https://github.com/bokwoon95/go-structured-query) - Type-safe SQL builder and struct mapper for Go.
*   [sqlf (‚≠ê98)](https://github.com/leporo/sqlf) - Fast SQL query builder.
*   [sqlingo (‚≠ê302)](https://github.com/lqs/sqlingo) - A lightweight DSL to build SQL in Go.
*   [sqrl (‚≠ê251)](https://github.com/elgris/sqrl) - SQL query builder, fork of Squirrel with improved performance.
*   [Squalus](https://gitlab.com/qosenergy/squalus) - Thin layer over the Go SQL package that makes it easier to perform queries.
*   [Squirrel (‚≠ê5.7k)](https://github.com/Masterminds/squirrel) - Go library that helps you build SQL queries.
*   [xo (‚≠ê3.3k)](https://github.com/knq/xo) - Generate idiomatic Go code for databases based on existing schema definitions or custom queries supporting PostgreSQL, MySQL, SQLite, Oracle, and Microsoft SQL Server.

### Date and Time

*   [carbon (‚≠ê3.1k)](https://github.com/golang-module/carbon) - A simple, semantic and developer-friendly golang package for datetime.
*   [carbon (‚≠ê751)](https://github.com/uniplaces/carbon) - Simple Time extension with a lot of util methods, ported from PHP Carbon library.
*   [cronrange (‚≠ê18)](https://github.com/1set/cronrange) - Parses Cron-style time range expressions, checks if the given time is within any ranges.
*   [date (‚≠ê108)](https://github.com/rickb777/date) - Augments Time for working with dates, date ranges, time spans, periods, and time-of-day.
*   [dateparse (‚≠ê1.8k)](https://github.com/araddon/dateparse) - Parse date's without knowing format in advance.
*   [durafmt (‚≠ê457)](https://github.com/hako/durafmt) - Time duration formatting library for Go.
*   [feiertage (‚≠ê43)](https://github.com/wlbr/feiertage) - Set of functions to calculate public holidays in Germany, incl. specialization on the states of Germany (Bundesl√§nder). Things like Easter, Pentecost, Thanksgiving...
*   [go-persian-calendar (‚≠ê150)](https://github.com/yaa110/go-persian-calendar) - The implementation of the Persian (Solar Hijri) Calendar in Go (golang).
*   [go-str2duration (‚≠ê70)](https://github.com/xhit/go-str2duration) - Convert string to duration. Support time.Duration returned string and more.
*   [go-sunrise (‚≠ê66)](https://github.com/nathan-osman/go-sunrise) - Calculate the sunrise and sunset times for a given location.
*   [go-week (‚≠ê8)](https://github.com/stoewer/go-week) - An efficient package to work with ISO8601 week dates.
*   [gostradamus (‚≠ê177)](https://github.com/bykof/gostradamus) - A Go package for working with dates.
*   [iso8601 (‚≠ê122)](https://github.com/relvacode/iso8601) - Efficiently parse ISO8601 date-times without regex.
*   [kair (‚≠ê25)](https://github.com/GuilhermeCaruso/kair) - Date and Time - Golang Formatting Library.
*   [now (‚≠ê4.1k)](https://github.com/jinzhu/now) - Now is a time toolkit for golang.
*   [NullTime (‚≠ê14)](https://github.com/kirillDanshin/nulltime) - Nullable `time.Time`.
*   [strftime (‚≠ê12)](https://github.com/awoodbeck/strftime) - C99-compatible strftime formatter.
*   [timespan (‚≠ê82)](https://github.com/SaidinWoT/timespan) - For interacting with intervals of time, defined as a start time and a duration.
*   [timeutil (‚≠ê191)](https://github.com/leekchan/timeutil) - Useful extensions (Timedelta, Strftime, ...) to the golang's time package.
*   [tuesday (‚≠ê12)](https://github.com/osteele/tuesday) - Ruby-compatible Strftime function.

### Distributed Systems

*   [arpc (‚≠ê725)](https://github.com/lesismal/arpc) - More effective network communication, support two-way-calling, notify, broadcast.
*   [celeriac (‚≠ê72)](https://github.com/svcavallar/celeriac.v1) - Library for adding support for interacting and monitoring Celery workers, tasks and events in Go.
*   [consistent (‚≠ê585)](https://github.com/buraksezer/consistent) - Consistent hashing with bounded loads.

*   [doublejump (‚≠ê88)](https://github.com/edwingeng/doublejump) - A revamped Google's jump consistent hash.
*   [dragonboat (‚≠ê4.6k)](https://github.com/lni/dragonboat) - A feature complete and high performance multi-group Raft library in Go.
*   [drmaa (‚≠ê43)](https://github.com/dgruber/drmaa) - Job submission library for cluster schedulers based on the DRMAA standard.

*   [emitter-io (‚≠ê3.5k)](https://github.com/emitter-io/emitter) - High performance, distributed, secure and low latency publish-subscribe platform built with MQTT, Websockets and love.
*   [failured (‚≠ê10)](https://github.com/andy2046/failured) - adaptive accrual failure detector for distributed systems.
*   [flowgraph (‚≠ê52)](https://github.com/vectaport/flowgraph) - flow-based programming package.
*   [gleam (‚≠ê3.2k)](https://github.com/chrislusf/gleam) - Fast and scalable distributed map/reduce system written in pure Go and Luajit, combining Go's high concurrency with Luajit's high performance, runs standalone or distributed.
*   [glow (‚≠ê3.1k)](https://github.com/chrislusf/glow) - Easy-to-Use scalable distributed big data processing, Map-Reduce, DAG execution, all in pure Go.
*   [gmsec (‚≠ê22)](https://github.com/gmsec/micro) - A Go distributed systems development framework.
*   [go-doudou (‚≠ê1.1k)](https://github.com/unionj-cloud/go-doudou) - A gossip protocol and OpenAPI 3.0 spec based decentralized microservice framework. Built-in go-doudou cli focusing on low-code and rapid dev can power up your productivity.
*   [go-health (‚≠ê671)](https://github.com/InVisionApp/go-health) - Library for enabling asynchronous dependency health checks in your service.
*   [go-jump (‚≠ê360)](https://github.com/dgryski/go-jump) - Port of Google's "Jump" Consistent Hash function.

*   [go-pdu (‚≠ê45)](https://github.com/pdupub/go-pdu) - A decentralized identity-based social network.
*   [go-sundheit (‚≠ê513)](https://github.com/AppsFlyer/go-sundheit) - A library built to provide support for defining async service health checks for golang services.
*   [go-zero (‚≠ê24k)](https://github.com/tal-tech/go-zero) - A web and rpc framework. It's born to ensure the stability of the busy sites with resilient design. Builtin goctl greatly improves the development productivity.
*   [gorpc (‚≠ê675)](https://github.com/valyala/gorpc) - Simple, fast and scalable RPC library for high load.
*   [grpc-go (‚≠ê18k)](https://github.com/grpc/grpc-go) - The Go language implementation of gRPC. HTTP/2 based RPC.

### Error Handling

*   [emperror (‚≠ê295)](https://github.com/emperror/emperror) - Error handling tools and best practices for Go libraries and applications.
*   [eris (‚≠ê1.3k)](https://github.com/rotisserie/eris) - A better way to handle, trace, and log errors in Go. Compatible with the standard error library and github.com/pkg/errors.
*   [errlog (‚≠ê443)](https://github.com/snwfdhmp/errlog) - Hackable package that determines responsible source code for an error (and some other fast-debugging features). Pluggable to any logger in-place.
*   [errors (‚≠ê174)](https://github.com/emperror/errors) - Drop-in replacement for the standard library errors package and github.com/pkg/errors. Provides various error handling primitives.
*   [errors (‚≠ê8k)](https://github.com/pkg/errors) - Package that provides simple error handling primitives.
*   [errors (‚≠ê5)](https://github.com/neuronlabs/errors) - Simple golang error handling with classification primitives.
*   [errors (‚≠ê8)](https://github.com/PumpkinSeed/errors) - The most simple error wrapper with awesome performance and minimal memory overhead.
*   [errorx (‚≠ê964)](https://github.com/joomcode/errorx) - A feature rich error package with stack traces, composition of errors and more.
*   [Falcon (‚≠ê9)](https://github.com/SonicRoshan/falcon) - A Simple Yet Highly Powerful Package For Error Handling.
*   [go-multierror (‚≠ê1.9k)](https://github.com/hashicorp/go-multierror) - Go (golang) package for representing a list of errors as a single error.
*   [tracerr (‚≠ê767)](https://github.com/ztrue/tracerr) - Golang errors with stack trace and source fragments.

*   [checksum (‚≠ê85)](https://github.com/codingsince1985/checksum) - Compute message digest, like MD5, SHA256, SHA1, CRC or BLAKE2s, for large files.

*   [go-decent-copy (‚≠ê19)](https://github.com/hugocarreira/go-decent-copy) - Copy files for humans.
*   [go-exiftool (‚≠ê166)](https://github.com/barasher/go-exiftool) - Go bindings for ExifTool, the well-known library used to extract as much metadata as possible (EXIF, IPTC, ...) from files (pictures, PDF, office, ...).
*   [go-gtfs (‚≠ê34)](https://github.com/artonge/go-gtfs) - Load gtfs files in go.
*   [gut/yos (‚≠ê26)](https://github.com/1set/gut) - Simple and reliable package for file operations like copy/move/diff/list on files, directories and symbolic links.
*   [higgs (‚≠ê15)](https://github.com/dastoori/higgs) - A tiny cross-platform Go library to hide/unhide files and directories.
*   [notify (‚≠ê816)](https://github.com/rjeczalik/notify) - File system event notification library with simple API, similar to os/signal.
*   [opc (‚≠ê74)](https://github.com/qmuntal/opc) - Load Open Packaging Conventions (OPC) files for Go.
*   [parquet (‚≠ê62)](https://github.com/parsyl/parquet) - Read and write [parquet](https://parquet.apache.org) files.
*   [pathtype (‚≠ê12)](https://github.com/jonchun/pathtype) - Treat paths as their own type instead of using strings.
*   [pdfcpu (‚≠ê4.9k)](https://github.com/pdfcpu/pdfcpu) - PDF processor.
*   [skywalker (‚≠ê87)](https://github.com/dixonwille/skywalker) - Package to allow one to concurrently go through a filesystem with ease.
*   [tarfs (‚≠ê51)](https://github.com/posener/tarfs) - Implementation of the [`FileSystem` interface](https://godoc.org/github.com/kr/fs#FileSystem) for tar files.
*   [todotxt (‚≠ê19)](https://github.com/1set/todotxt) - Go library for Gina Trapani's [*todo.txt*](http://todotxt.org/) files, supports parsing and manipulating of task lists in the [*todo.txt* format](https://github.com/todotxt/todo.txt).
*   [vfs (‚≠ê217)](https://github.com/C2FO/vfs) - A pluggable, extensible, and opinionated set of filesystem functionality for Go across a number of filesystem types such as os, S3, and GCS.

### Generators

*   [generis (‚≠ê38)](https://github.com/senselogic/GENERIS) - Code generation tool providing generics, free-form macros, conditional compilation and HTML templating.
*   [go-enum (‚≠ê468)](https://github.com/abice/go-enum) - Code generation for enums from code comments.
*   [go-linq (‚≠ê3.3k)](https://github.com/ahmetalpbalkan/go-linq) - .NET LINQ-like query methods for Go.
*   [goderive (‚≠ê1.1k)](https://github.com/awalterschulze/goderive) - Derives functions from input types.
*   [gotype (‚≠ê53)](https://github.com/wzshiming/gotype) - Golang source code parsing, usage like reflect package.
*   [goverter (‚≠ê221)](https://github.com/jmattheis/goverter) - Generate converters by defining an interface.
*   [GoWrap (‚≠ê738)](https://github.com/hexdigest/gowrap) - Generate decorators for Go interfaces using simple templates.
*   [interfaces (‚≠ê376)](https://github.com/rjeczalik/interfaces) - Command line tool for generating interface definitions.
*   [jennifer (‚≠ê2.8k)](https://github.com/dave/jennifer) - Generate arbitrary Go code without templates.
*   [typeregistry (‚≠ê17)](https://github.com/xiaoxin01/typeregistry) - A library to create type dynamically.

### Geographic

*   [geoserver (‚≠ê81)](https://github.com/hishamkaram/geoserver) - geoserver Is a Go Package For Manipulating a GeoServer Instance via the GeoServer REST API.

*   [osm (‚≠ê273)](https://github.com/paulmach/osm) - Library for reading, writing and working with OpenStreetMap data and APIs.
*   [pbf (‚≠ê43)](https://github.com/maguro/pbf) - OpenStreetMap PBF golang encoder/decoder.

*   [simplefeatures (‚≠ê79)](https://github.com/peterstace/simplefeatures) - simplesfeatures is a 2D geometry library that provides Go types that model geometries, as well as algorithms that operate on them.

*   [WGS84 (‚≠ê97)](https://github.com/wroge/wgs84) - Library for Coordinate Conversion and Transformation (ETRS89, OSGB36, NAD83, RGF93, Web Mercator, UTM).

### Goroutines

*   [ants (‚≠ê10k)](https://github.com/panjf2000/ants) - A high-performance and low-cost goroutine pool in Go.
*   [artifex (‚≠ê165)](https://github.com/borderstech/artifex) - Simple in-memory job queue for Golang using worker-based dispatching.
*   [async (‚≠ê112)](https://github.com/reugn/async) - An alternative sync library for Go (Future, Promise, Locks).
*   [async (‚≠ê119)](https://github.com/studiosol/async) - A safe way to execute functions asynchronously, recovering them in case of panic.
*   [breaker (‚≠ê14)](https://github.com/kamilsk/breaker) - Flexible mechanism to make execution flow interruptible.
*   [channelify (‚≠ê27)](https://github.com/ddelizia/channelify) - Transform your function to return channels for easy and powerful parallel processing.
*   [concurrency-limiter (‚≠ê12)](https://github.com/vivek-ng/concurrency-limiter) - Concurrency limiter with support for timeouts , dynamic priority and context cancellation of goroutines.
*   [conexec (‚≠ê13)](https://github.com/ITcathyh/conexec) - A concurrent toolkit to help execute funcs concurrently in an efficient and safe way. It supports specifying the overall timeout to avoid blocking and uses goroutine pool to improve efficiency.
*   [cyclicbarrier (‚≠ê122)](https://github.com/marusama/cyclicbarrier) - CyclicBarrier for golang.
*   [execpool (‚≠ê14)](https://github.com/hexdigest/execpool) - A pool built around exec.Cmd that spins up a given number of processes in advance and attaches stdin and stdout to them when needed. Very similar to FastCGI or Apache Prefork MPM but works for any command.
*   [go-floc (‚≠ê261)](https://github.com/workanator/go-floc) - Orchestrate goroutines with ease.
*   [go-flow (‚≠ê206)](https://github.com/kamildrazkiewicz/go-flow) - Control goroutines execution order.
*   [go-tools/multithreading (‚≠ê11)](https://github.com/nikhilsaraf/go-tools) - Manage a pool of goroutines using this lightweight library with a simple API.
*   [go-trylock (‚≠ê33)](https://github.com/subchen/go-trylock) - TryLock support on read-write lock for Golang.
*   [go-waitgroup (‚≠ê38)](https://github.com/pieterclaerhout/go-waitgroup) - Like `sync.WaitGroup` with error handling and concurrency control.
*   [go-workers (‚≠ê155)](https://github.com/catmullet/go-workers) - Easily and safely run workers for large data processing pipelines.
*   [goccm (‚≠ê63)](https://github.com/zenthangplus/goccm) - Go Concurrency Manager package limits the number of goroutines that allowed to run concurrently.
*   [gohive (‚≠ê44)](https://github.com/loveleshsharma/gohive) - A highly performant and easy to use Goroutine pool for Go.
*   [gollback (‚≠ê106)](https://github.com/vardius/gollback) - asynchronous simple function utilities, for managing execution of closures and callbacks.
*   [gowl (‚≠ê52)](https://github.com/hamed-yousefi/gowl) - Gowl is a process management and process monitoring tool at once. An infinite worker pool gives you the ability to control the pool and processes and monitor their status.
*   [goworker (‚≠ê2.7k)](https://github.com/benmanns/goworker) - goworker is a Go-based background worker.
*   [gowp (‚≠ê441)](https://github.com/xxjwxc/gowp) - gowp is concurrency limiting goroutine pool.
*   [gpool (‚≠ê86)](https://github.com/Sherifabdlnaby/gpool) - manages a resizeable pool of context-aware goroutines to bound concurrency.
*   [grpool (‚≠ê726)](https://github.com/ivpusic/grpool) - Lightweight Goroutine pool.
*   [hands (‚≠ê10)](https://github.com/duanckham/hands) - A process controller used to control the execution and return strategies of multiple goroutines.
*   [Hunch (‚≠ê95)](https://github.com/AaronJan/Hunch) - Hunch provides functions like: `All`, `First`, `Retry`, `Waterfall` etc., that makes asynchronous flow control more intuitive.
*   [kyoo (‚≠ê40)](https://github.com/dirkaholic/kyoo) - Provides an unlimited job queue and concurrent worker pools.
*   [neilotoole/errgroup (‚≠ê145)](https://github.com/neilotoole/errgroup) - Drop-in alternative to `sync/errgroup`, limited to a pool of N worker goroutines.
*   [nursery (‚≠ê61)](https://github.com/arunsworld/nursery) - Structured concurrency in Go.
*   [oversight](https://cirello.io/oversight) - Oversight is a complete implementation of the Erlang supervision trees.
*   [parallel-fn (‚≠ê35)](https://github.com/rafaeljesus/parallel-fn) - Run functions in parallel.
*   [pond (‚≠ê795)](https://github.com/alitto/pond) - Minimalistic and High-performance goroutine worker pool written in Go.
*   [pool (‚≠ê713)](https://github.com/go-playground/pool) - Limited consumer goroutine or unlimited goroutine pool for easier goroutine handling and cancellation.
*   [queue (‚≠ê14)](https://github.com/AnikHasibul/queue) - Gives you a `sync.WaitGroup` like queue group accessibility. Helps you to throttle and limit goroutines, wait for the end of the all goroutines and much more.
*   [routine (‚≠ê56)](https://github.com/x-mod/routine) - go routine control with context, support: Main, Go, Pool and some useful Executors.
*   [semaphore (‚≠ê95)](https://github.com/kamilsk/semaphore) - Semaphore pattern implementation with timeout of lock/unlock operations based on channel and context.
*   [semaphore (‚≠ê160)](https://github.com/marusama/semaphore) - Fast resizable semaphore implementation based on CAS (faster than channel-based semaphore implementations).
*   [stl (‚≠ê26)](https://github.com/ssgreg/stl) - Software transactional locks based on Software Transactional Memory (STM) concurrency control mechanism.
*   [threadpool (‚≠ê89)](https://github.com/shettyh/threadpool) - Golang threadpool implementation.
*   [tunny (‚≠ê3.6k)](https://github.com/Jeffail/tunny) - Goroutine pool for golang.
*   [worker-pool (‚≠ê87)](https://github.com/vardius/worker-pool) - goworker is a Go simple async worker pool.
*   [workerpool (‚≠ê1.1k)](https://github.com/gammazero/workerpool) - Goroutine pool that limits the concurrency of task execution, not the number of tasks queued.

*   [robotgo (‚≠ê8.3k)](https://github.com/go-vgo/robotgo) - Go Native cross-platform GUI system automation. Control the mouse, keyboard and other.
*   [systray (‚≠ê2.7k)](https://github.com/getlantern/systray) - Cross platform Go library to place an icon and menu in the notification area.
*   [trayhost (‚≠ê237)](https://github.com/shurcooL/trayhost) - Cross-platform Go library to place an icon in the host operating system's taskbar.
*   [zenity (‚≠ê449)](https://github.com/ncruces/zenity) - Cross-platform Go library and CLI to create simple dialogs that interact graphically with the user.

### Job Scheduler

*   [cheek (‚≠ê73)](https://github.com/datarootsio/cheek) - A simple crontab like scheduler that aims to offer a KISS approach to job scheduling.
*   [clockwerk (‚≠ê135)](https://github.com/onatm/clockwerk) - Go package to schedule periodic jobs using a simple, fluent syntax.
*   [cronticker (‚≠ê8)](https://github.com/krayzpipes/cronticker) - A ticker implementation to support cron schedules.
*   [go-cron (‚≠ê216)](https://github.com/rk/go-cron) - Simple Cron library for go that can execute closures or functions at varying intervals, from once a second to once a year on a specific date and time. Primarily for web applications and long running daemons.
*   [go-quartz (‚≠ê1.2k)](https://github.com/reugn/go-quartz) - Simple, zero-dependency scheduling library for Go.
*   [gocron (‚≠ê3.1k)](https://github.com/go-co-op/gocron) - Easy and fluent Go job scheduling. This is an actively maintained fork of [jasonlvhit/gocron (‚≠ê3.2k)](https://github.com/jasonlvhit/gocron).
*   [gron (‚≠ê963)](https://github.com/roylee0704/gron) - Define time-based tasks using a simple Go API and Gron‚Äôs scheduler will run them accordingly.
*   [gronx (‚≠ê260)](https://github.com/adhocore/gronx) - Cron expression parser, task runner and daemon consuming crontab like task list.
*   [JobRunner (‚≠ê955)](https://github.com/bamzi/jobrunner) - Smart and featureful cron job scheduler with job queuing and live monitoring built in.
*   [jobs (‚≠ê495)](https://github.com/albrow/jobs) - Persistent and flexible background jobs library.
*   [leprechaun (‚≠ê94)](https://github.com/kilgaloon/leprechaun) - Job scheduler that supports webhooks, crons and classic scheduling.
*   [sched (‚≠ê26)](https://github.com/romshark/sched) - A job scheduler with the ability to fast-forward time.
*   [scheduler (‚≠ê421)](https://github.com/carlescere/scheduler) - Cronjobs scheduling made easy.
*   [tasks (‚≠ê149)](https://github.com/madflojo/tasks) - An easy to use in-process scheduler for recurring tasks in Go.

### JSON

*   [ajson (‚≠ê160)](https://github.com/spyzhov/ajson) - Abstract JSON for golang with JSONPath support.
*   [ask (‚≠ê25)](https://github.com/simonnilsson/ask) - Easy access to nested values in maps and slices. Works in combination with encoding/json and other packages that "Unmarshal" arbitrary data into Go data-types.
*   [dynjson (‚≠ê14)](https://github.com/cocoonspace/dynjson) - Client-customizable JSON formats for dynamic APIs.
*   [ej (‚≠ê9)](https://github.com/lucassscaravelli/ej) - Write and read JSON from different sources succinctly.
*   [epoch (‚≠ê12)](https://github.com/vtopc/epoch) - Contains primitives for marshaling/unmarshaling Unix timestamp/epoch to/from build-in time.Time type in JSON.
*   [fastjson (‚≠ê1.9k)](https://github.com/valyala/fastjson) - Fast JSON parser and validator for Go. No custom structs, no code generation, no reflection.
*   [gjo (‚≠ê120)](https://github.com/skanehira/gjo) - Small utility to create JSON objects.
*   [GJSON (‚≠ê12k)](https://github.com/tidwall/gjson) - Get a JSON value with one line of code.
*   [go-jsonerror (‚≠ê13)](https://github.com/ddymko/go-jsonerror) - Go-JsonError is meant to allow us to easily create json response errors that follow the JsonApi spec.
*   [go-respond (‚≠ê51)](https://github.com/nicklaw5/go-respond) - Go package for handling common HTTP JSON responses.
*   [gojq (‚≠ê186)](https://github.com/elgs/gojq) - JSON query in Golang.
*   [gojson (‚≠ê2.6k)](https://github.com/ChimeraCoder/gojson) - Automatically generate Go (golang) struct definitions from example JSON.
*   [JayDiff (‚≠ê95)](https://github.com/yazgazan/jaydiff) - JSON diff utility written in Go.
*   [jettison (‚≠ê146)](https://github.com/wI2L/jettison) - Fast and flexible JSON encoder for Go.
*   [jscan (‚≠ê28)](https://github.com/romshark/jscan) - High performance zero-allocation JSON iterator.
*   [JSON-to-Go](https://mholt.github.io/json-to-go/) - Convert JSON to Go struct.
*   [JSON-to-Proto](https://json-to-proto.github.io/) - Convert JSON to Protobuf online.
*   [json2go (‚≠ê114)](https://github.com/m-zajac/json2go) - Advanced JSON to Go struct conversion. Provides package that can parse multiple JSON documents and create struct to fit them all.
*   [jsonapi-errors (‚≠ê13)](https://github.com/AmuzaTkts/jsonapi-errors) - Go bindings based on the JSON API errors reference.
*   [jsoncolor (‚≠ê28)](https://github.com/neilotoole/jsoncolor) - Drop-in replacement for `encoding/json` that outputs colorized JSON.
*   [jsondiff (‚≠ê236)](https://github.com/wI2L/jsondiff) - JSON diff library for Go based on RFC6902 (JSON Patch).
*   [jsonf (‚≠ê64)](https://github.com/miolini/jsonf) - Console tool for highlighted formatting and struct query fetching JSON.
*   [jsongo (‚≠ê109)](https://github.com/ricardolonga/jsongo) - Fluent API to make it easier to create Json objects.
*   [jsonhal (‚≠ê13)](https://github.com/RichardKnop/jsonhal) - Simple Go package to make custom structs marshal into HAL compatible JSON responses.
*   [jsonic (‚≠ê8)](https://github.com/sinhashubham95/jsonic) - Utilities to handle and query JSON without defining structs in a type safe manner.
*   [jzon (‚≠ê11)](https://github.com/zerosnake0/jzon) - JSON library with standard compatible API/behavior.
*   [kazaam (‚≠ê252)](https://github.com/Qntfy/kazaam) - API for arbitrary transformation of JSON documents.
*   [mapslice-json (‚≠ê15)](https://github.com/mickep76/mapslice-json) - Go MapSlice for ordered marshal/ unmarshal of maps in JSON.
*   [mp (‚≠ê46)](https://github.com/sanbornm/mp) - Simple cli email parser. It currently takes stdin and outputs JSON.
*   [OjG (‚≠ê584)](https://github.com/ohler55/ojg) - Optimized JSON for Go is a high performance parser with a variety of additional JSON tools including JSONPath.
*   [omg.jsonparser (‚≠ê4)](https://github.com/dedalqq/omg.jsonparser) - Simple JSON parser with validation by condition via golang struct fields tags.
*   [ujson (‚≠ê64)](https://github.com/olvrng/ujson) - Fast and minimal JSON parser and transformer that works on unstructured JSON.
*   [vjson (‚≠ê33)](https://github.com/miladibra10/vjson) - Go package for validating JSON objects with declaring a JSON schema with fluent API.

### Logging

*   [distillog (‚≠ê31)](https://github.com/amoghe/distillog) - distilled levelled logging (think of it as stdlib + log levels).
*   [glg (‚≠ê180)](https://github.com/kpango/glg) - glg is simple and fast leveled logging library for Go.
*   [glo (‚≠ê15)](https://github.com/lajosbencz/glo) - PHP Monolog inspired logging facility with identical severity levels.
*   [glog (‚≠ê3.3k)](https://github.com/golang/glog) - Leveled execution logs for Go.
*   [go-cronowriter (‚≠ê54)](https://github.com/utahta/go-cronowriter) - Simple writer that rotate log files automatically based on current date and time, like cronolog.
*   [go-log (‚≠ê13)](https://github.com/subchen/go-log) - Simple and configurable Logging in Go, with level, formatters and writers.
*   [go-log (‚≠ê33)](https://github.com/siddontang/go-log) - Log lib supports level and multi handlers.
*   [go-log (‚≠ê40)](https://github.com/ian-kent/go-log) - Log4j implementation in Go.
*   [go-logger (‚≠ê284)](https://github.com/apsdehal/go-logger) - Simple logger of Go Programs, with level handlers.
*   [gologger (‚≠ê41)](https://github.com/sadlil/gologger) - Simple easy to use log lib for go, logs in Colored Console, Simple Console, File or Elasticsearch.
*   [gomol (‚≠ê19)](https://github.com/aphistic/gomol) - Multiple-output, structured logging for Go with extensible logging outputs.
*   [gone/log (‚≠ê45)](https://github.com/One-com/gone/tree/master/log) - Fast, extendable, full-featured, std-lib source compatible log library.
*   [httpretty (‚≠ê297)](https://github.com/henvic/httpretty) - Pretty-prints your regular HTTP requests on your terminal for debugging (similar to http.DumpRequest).
*   [journald (‚≠ê34)](https://github.com/ssgreg/journald) - Go implementation of systemd Journal's native API for logging.
*   [kemba (‚≠ê10)](https://github.com/clok/kemba) - A tiny debug logging tool inspired by [debug (‚≠ê11k)](https://github.com/visionmedia/debug), great for CLI tools and applications.
*   [log (‚≠ê10)](https://github.com/aerogo/log) - An O(1) logging system that allows you to connect one log to multiple writers (e.g. stdout, a file and a TCP connection).
*   [log (‚≠ê1.3k)](https://github.com/apex/log) - Structured logging package for Go.
*   [log (‚≠ê284)](https://github.com/go-playground/log) - Simple, configurable and scalable Structured Logging for Go.
*   [log (‚≠ê26)](https://github.com/teris-io/log) - Structured log interface for Go cleanly separates logging facade from its implementation.
*   [log-voyage (‚≠ê94)](https://github.com/firstrow/logvoyage) - Full-featured logging saas written in golang.
*   [log15 (‚≠ê1.1k)](https://github.com/inconshreveable/log15) - Simple, powerful logging for Go.
*   [logdump (‚≠ê11)](https://github.com/ewwwwwqm/logdump) - Package for multi-level logging.
*   [logex (‚≠ê40)](https://github.com/chzyer/logex) - Golang log lib, supports tracking and level, wrap by standard log lib.
*   [logger (‚≠ê157)](https://github.com/azer/logger) - Minimalistic logging library for Go.
*   [logmatic (‚≠ê16)](https://github.com/borderstech/logmatic) - Colorized logger for Golang with dynamic log level configuration.
*   [logo (‚≠ê11)](https://github.com/mbndr/logo) - Golang logger to different configurable writers.
*   [logrus (‚≠ê22k)](https://github.com/Sirupsen/logrus) - Structured logger for Go.
*   [logrusiowriter (‚≠ê14)](https://github.com/cabify/logrusiowriter) - `io.Writer` implementation using [logrus (‚≠ê22k)](https://github.com/sirupsen/logrus) logger.
*   [logrusly (‚≠ê28)](https://github.com/sebest/logrusly) - [logrus (‚≠ê22k)](https://github.com/sirupsen/logrus) plug-in to send errors to a [Loggly](https://www.loggly.com/).
*   [logur (‚≠ê190)](https://github.com/logur/logur) - An opinionated logger interface and collection of logging best practices with adapters and integrations for well-known libraries ([logrus (‚≠ê22k)](https://github.com/sirupsen/logrus), [go-kit log (‚≠ê25k)](https://github.com/go-kit/kit/tree/master/log), [zap (‚≠ê18k)](https://github.com/uber-go/zap), [zerolog (‚≠ê8k)](https://github.com/rs/zerolog), etc).
*   [logutils (‚≠ê347)](https://github.com/hashicorp/logutils) - Utilities for slightly better logging in Go (Golang) extending the standard logger.
*   [logxi (‚≠ê349)](https://github.com/mgutz/logxi) - 12-factor app logger that is fast and makes you happy.
*   [lumberjack (‚≠ê4k)](https://github.com/natefinch/lumberjack) - Simple rolling logger, implements io.WriteCloser.
*   [mlog (‚≠ê31)](https://github.com/jbrodriguez/mlog) - Simple logging module for go, with 5 levels, an optional rotating logfile feature and stdout/stderr output.
*   [noodlog (‚≠ê44)](https://github.com/gyozatech/noodlog) - Parametrized JSON logging library which lets you obfuscate sensitive data and marshal any kind of content. No more printed pointers instead of values, nor escape chars for the JSON strings.
*   [onelog (‚≠ê405)](https://github.com/francoispqt/onelog) - Onelog is a dead simple but very efficient JSON logger. It is the fastest JSON logger out there in all scenarios. Also, it is one of the logger with the lowest allocation.
*   [ozzo-log (‚≠ê121)](https://github.com/go-ozzo/ozzo-log) - High performance logging supporting log severity, categorization, and filtering. Can send filtered log messages to various targets (e.g. console, network, mail).
*   [rollingwriter (‚≠ê263)](https://github.com/arthurkiller/rollingWriter) - RollingWriter is an auto-rotate `io.Writer` implementation with multi policies to provide log file rotation.
*   [seelog (‚≠ê1.6k)](https://github.com/cihub/seelog) - Logging functionality with flexible dispatching, filtering, and formatting.
*   [spew (‚≠ê5.6k)](https://github.com/davecgh/go-spew) - Implements a deep pretty printer for Go data structures to aid in debugging.
*   [stdlog (‚≠ê47)](https://github.com/alexcesaro/log) - Stdlog is an object-oriented library providing leveled logging. It is very useful for cron jobs.
*   [structy/log (‚≠ê5)](https://github.com/structy/log) - A simple to use log system, minimalist but with features for debugging and differentiation of messages.
*   [tail (‚≠ê2.5k)](https://github.com/hpcloud/tail) - Go package striving to emulate the features of the BSD tail program.
*   [xlog (‚≠ê8)](https://github.com/xfxdev/xlog) - Plugin architecture and flexible log system for Go, with level ctrl, multiple log target and custom log format.
*   [xlog (‚≠ê137)](https://github.com/rs/xlog) - Structured logger for `net/context` aware HTTP handlers with flexible dispatching.
*   [yell (‚≠ê1)](https://github.com/jfcg/yell) - Yet another minimalistic logging library.
*   [zap (‚≠ê18k)](https://github.com/uber-go/zap) - Fast, structured, leveled logging in Go.
*   [zerolog (‚≠ê8k)](https://github.com/rs/zerolog) - Zero-allocation JSON logger.
*   [zkits-logger (‚≠ê24)](https://github.com/edoger/zkits-logger) - A powerful zero-dependency JSON logger.

### Messaging

*   [ami (‚≠ê26)](https://github.com/kak-tus/ami) - Go client to reliable queues based on Redis Cluster Streams.
*   [amqp (‚≠ê812)](https://github.com/rabbitmq/amqp091-go) - Go RabbitMQ Client Library.
*   [APNs2 (‚≠ê2.8k)](https://github.com/sideshow/apns2) - HTTP/2 Apple Push Notification provider for Go ‚Äî Send push notifications to iOS, tvOS, Safari and OSX apps.
*   [Asynq (‚≠ê5.8k)](https://github.com/hibiken/asynq) - A simple, reliable, and efficient distributed task queue for Go built on top of Redis.
*   [Beaver (‚≠ê1.4k)](https://github.com/Clivern/Beaver) - A real time messaging server to build a scalable in-app notifications, multiplayer games, chat apps in web and mobile apps.
*   [Benthos (‚≠ê6k)](https://github.com/Jeffail/benthos) - A message streaming bridge between a range of protocols.
*   [Bus (‚≠ê293)](https://github.com/mustafaturan/bus) - Minimalist message bus implementation for internal communication.
*   [Centrifugo (‚≠ê7k)](https://github.com/centrifugal/centrifugo) - Real-time messaging (Websockets or SockJS) server in Go.
*   [Chanify (‚≠ê1k)](https://github.com/chanify/chanify) - A push notification server send message to your iOS devices.
*   [Commander (‚≠ê64)](https://github.com/jeroenrinzema/commander) - A high-level event driven consumer/producer supporting various "dialects" such as Apache Kafka.
*   [Confluent Kafka Golang Client (‚≠ê3.9k)](https://github.com/confluentinc/confluent-kafka-go) - confluent-kafka-go is Confluent's Golang client for Apache Kafka and the Confluent Platform.
*   [dbus (‚≠ê839)](https://github.com/godbus/dbus) - Native Go bindings for D-Bus.
*   [drone-line (‚≠ê79)](https://github.com/appleboy/drone-line) - Sending [Line](https://at.line.me/en) notifications using a binary, docker or Drone CI.
*   [emitter (‚≠ê450)](https://github.com/olebedev/emitter) - Emits events using Go way, with wildcard, predicates, cancellation possibilities and many other good wins.
*   [event (‚≠ê53)](https://github.com/agoalofalife/event) - Implementation of the pattern observer.
*   [EventBus (‚≠ê1.4k)](https://github.com/asaskevich/EventBus) - The lightweight event bus with async compatibility.
*   [gaurun-client (‚≠ê11)](https://github.com/osamingo/gaurun-client) - Gaurun Client written in Go.
*   [Glue (‚≠ê408)](https://github.com/desertbit/glue) - Robust Go and Javascript Socket Library (Alternative to Socket.io).
*   [go-mq (‚≠ê84)](https://github.com/cheshir/go-mq) - RabbitMQ client with declarative configuration.
*   [go-notify (‚≠ê65)](https://github.com/TheCreeper/go-notify) - Native implementation of the freedesktop notification spec.
*   [go-nsq (‚≠ê2.4k)](https://github.com/nsqio/go-nsq) - the official Go package for NSQ.
*   [go-res (‚≠ê62)](https://github.com/jirenius/go-res) - Package for building REST/real-time services where clients are synchronized seamlessly, using NATS and Resgate.
*   [go-socket.io (‚≠ê5.1k)](https://github.com/googollee/go-socket.io) - socket.io library for golang, a realtime application framework.
*   [go-vitotrol (‚≠ê22)](https://github.com/maxatome/go-vitotrol) - Client library to Viessmann Vitotrol web service.
*   [Gollum (‚≠ê927)](https://github.com/trivago/gollum) - A n:m multiplexer that gathers messages from different sources and broadcasts them to a set of destinations.
*   [golongpoll (‚≠ê626)](https://github.com/jcuga/golongpoll) - HTTP longpoll server library that makes web pub-sub simple.
*   [gopush-cluster (‚≠ê2.1k)](https://github.com/Terry-Mao/gopush-cluster) - gopush-cluster is a go push server cluster.
*   [gorush (‚≠ê7k)](https://github.com/appleboy/gorush) - Push notification server using [APNs2 (‚≠ê2.8k)](https://github.com/sideshow/apns2) and google [GCM (‚≠ê103)](https://github.com/google/go-gcm).
*   [gosd (‚≠ê21)](https://github.com/alexsniffin/gosd) - A library for scheduling when to dispatch a message to a channel.
*   [guble (‚≠ê155)](https://github.com/smancke/guble) - Messaging server using push notifications (Google Firebase Cloud Messaging, Apple Push Notification services, SMS) as well as websockets, a REST API, featuring distributed operation and message-persistence.
*   [hare (‚≠ê53)](https://github.com/leozz37/hare) - A user friendly library for sending messages and listening to TCP sockets.
*   [hub (‚≠ê129)](https://github.com/leandro-lugaresi/hub) - A Message/Event Hub for Go applications, using publish/subscribe pattern with support for alias like rabbitMQ exchanges.
*   [jazz (‚≠ê17)](https://github.com/socifi/jazz) - A simple RabbitMQ abstraction layer for queue administration and publishing and consuming of messages.
*   [machinery (‚≠ê6.8k)](https://github.com/RichardKnop/machinery) - Asynchronous task queue/job queue based on distributed message passing.
*   [mangos (‚≠ê582)](https://github.com/nanomsg/mangos) - Pure go implementation of the Nanomsg ("Scalability Protocols") with transport interoperability.
*   [melody (‚≠ê3k)](https://github.com/olahol/melody) - Minimalist framework for dealing with websocket sessions, includes broadcasting and automatic ping/pong handling.
*   [Mercure (‚≠ê3.3k)](https://github.com/dunglas/mercure) - Server and library to dispatch server-sent updates using the Mercure protocol (built on top of Server-Sent Events).
*   [messagebus (‚≠ê246)](https://github.com/vardius/message-bus) - messagebus is a Go simple async message bus, perfect for using as event bus when doing event sourcing, CQRS, DDD.
*   [NATS Go Client (‚≠ê4.5k)](https://github.com/nats-io/nats) - Lightweight and high performance publish-subscribe and distributed queueing messaging system - this is the Go library.
*   [nsq-event-bus (‚≠ê75)](https://github.com/rafaeljesus/nsq-event-bus) - A tiny wrapper around NSQ topic and channel.
*   [oplog (‚≠ê114)](https://github.com/dailymotion/oplog) - Generic oplog/replication system for REST APIs.
*   [pubsub (‚≠ê388)](https://github.com/tuxychandru/pubsub) - Simple pubsub package for go.
*   [rabbus (‚≠ê96)](https://github.com/rafaeljesus/rabbus) - A tiny wrapper over amqp exchanges and queues.
*   [rabtap (‚≠ê236)](https://github.com/jandelgado/rabtap) - RabbitMQ swiss army knife cli app.
*   [RapidMQ (‚≠ê65)](https://github.com/sybrexsys/RapidMQ) - RapidMQ is a lightweight and reliable library for managing of the local messages queue.
*   [redisqueue (‚≠ê108)](https://github.com/robinjoseph08/redisqueue) - redisqueue provides a producer and consumer of a queue that uses Redis streams.
*   [rmqconn (‚≠ê20)](https://github.com/sbabiv/rmqconn) - RabbitMQ Reconnection. Wrapper over amqp.Connection and amqp.Dial. Allowing to do a reconnection when the connection is broken before forcing the call to the Close () method to be closed.
*   [sarama (‚≠ê9.9k)](https://github.com/Shopify/sarama) - Go library for Apache Kafka.
*   [Uniqush-Push (‚≠ê1.5k)](https://github.com/uniqush/uniqush-push) - Redis backed unified push service for server-side notifications to mobile devices.
*   [zmq4 (‚≠ê1k)](https://github.com/pebbe/zmq4) - Go interface to ZeroMQ version 4. Also available for [version 3 (‚≠ê132)](https://github.com/pebbe/zmq3) and [version 2 (‚≠ê18)](https://github.com/pebbe/zmq2).

### Dependency Injection

*   [alice (‚≠ê52)](https://github.com/magic003/alice) - Additive dependency injection container for Golang.
*   [di (‚≠ê178)](https://github.com/goava/di) - A dependency injection container for go programming language.
*   [dig (‚≠ê3.1k)](https://github.com/uber-go/dig) - A reflection based dependency injection toolkit for Go.
*   [dingo (‚≠ê162)](https://github.com/i-love-flamingo/dingo) - A dependency injection toolkit for Go, based on Guice.
*   [fx (‚≠ê3.8k)](https://github.com/uber-go/fx) - A dependency injection based application framework for Go (built on top of dig).
*   [gocontainer (‚≠ê18)](https://github.com/vardius/gocontainer) - Simple Dependency Injection Container.
*   [goioc/di (‚≠ê255)](https://github.com/goioc/di) - Spring-inspired Dependency Injection Container.
*   [google/wire (‚≠ê10k)](https://github.com/google/wire) - Automated Initialization in Go.
*   [HnH/di (‚≠ê6)](https://github.com/HnH/di) - DI container library that is focused on clean API and flexibility.
*   [kinit (‚≠ê9)](https://github.com/go-kata/kinit) - Customizable dependency injection container with the global mode, cascade initialization and panic-safe finalization.
*   [linker (‚≠ê35)](https://github.com/logrange/linker) - A reflection based dependency injection and inversion of control library with components lifecycle support.
*   [wire (‚≠ê37)](https://github.com/Fs02/wire) - Strict Runtime Dependency Injection for Golang.

### Project Layout

*   [ardanlabs/service (‚≠ê2.7k)](https://github.com/ardanlabs/service) - A [starter kit (‚≠ê2.7k)](https://github.com/ardanlabs/service/wiki) for building production grade scalable web service applications.
*   [cookiecutter-golang (‚≠ê594)](https://github.com/lacion/cookiecutter-golang) - A Go application boilerplate template for quick starting projects following production best practices.
*   [go-sample (‚≠ê119)](https://github.com/zitryss/go-sample) - A sample layout for Go application projects with the real code.
*   [go-starter (‚≠ê318)](https://github.com/allaboutapps/go-starter) - An opinionated production-ready RESTful JSON backend template, highly integrated with VSCode DevContainers.
*   [go-todo-backend (‚≠ê213)](https://github.com/Fs02/go-todo-backend) - Go Todo Backend example using modular project layout for product microservice.
*   [gobase (‚≠ê46)](https://github.com/wajox/gobase) - A simple skeleton for golang application with basic setup for real golang application.
*   [golang-standards/project-layout (‚≠ê39k)](https://github.com/golang-standards/project-layout) - Set of common historical and emerging project layout patterns in the Go ecosystem. Note: despite the org-name they do not represent official golang standards, see [this issue (‚≠ê39k)](https://github.com/golang-standards/project-layout/issues/117) for more information. Nonetheless, some may find the layout useful.
*   [golang-templates/seed (‚≠ê370)](https://github.com/golang-templates/seed) - Go application GitHub repository template.
*   [insidieux/inizio (‚≠ê15)](https://github.com/insidieux/inizio) - Golang project layout generator with plugins.
*   [modern-go-application (‚≠ê1.5k)](https://github.com/sagikazarmark/modern-go-application) - Go application boilerplate and example applying modern practices.
*   [scaffold (‚≠ê137)](https://github.com/catchplay/scaffold) - Scaffold generates a starter Go project layout. Lets you focus on business logic implemented.
*   [wangyoucao577/go-project-layout (‚≠ê20)](https://github.com/wangyoucao577/go-project-layout) - Set of practices and discussions on how to structure Go project layout.

### Strings

*   [xstrings (‚≠ê1.2k)](https://github.com/huandu/xstrings) - Collection of useful string functions ported from other languages.

### Morphological Analyzers

*   [go-stem (‚≠ê75)](https://github.com/agonopol/go-stem) - Implementation of the porter stemming algorithm.

*   [gosentiwordnet (‚≠ê10)](https://github.com/dinopuguh/gosentiwordnet) - Sentiment analyzer using sentiwordnet lexicon in Go.
*   [govader (‚≠ê34)](https://github.com/jonreiter/govader) - Go implementation of [VADER Sentiment Analysis (‚≠ê3.9k)](https://github.com/cjhutto/vaderSentiment).
*   [kagome (‚≠ê713)](https://github.com/ikawaha/kagome) - JP morphological analyzer written in pure Go.
*   [libtextcat (‚≠ê12)](https://github.com/goodsign/libtextcat) - Cgo binding for libtextcat C library. Guaranteed compatibility with version 2.2.
*   [nlp (‚≠ê379)](https://github.com/Shixzie/nlp) - Extract values from strings and fill your structs with nlp.
*   [nlp (‚≠ê402)](https://github.com/james-bowman/nlp) - Go Natural Language Processing library supporting LSA (Latent Semantic Analysis).
*   [paicehusk (‚≠ê29)](https://github.com/rookii/paicehusk) - Golang implementation of the Paice/Husk Stemming Algorithm.

*   [porter2 (‚≠ê46)](https://github.com/zhenjl/porter2) - Really fast Porter 2 stemmer.
*   [RAKE.go (‚≠ê97)](https://github.com/afjoseph/RAKE.Go) - Go port of the Rapid Automatic Keyword Extraction Algorithm (RAKE).
